# Variations – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32692978437005-Variations#page-container)

Transform your images with simple tweaks or creative overhauls using variations.

### Transform your images with simple tweaks or creative overhauls using Variations!

![variations-header.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32694022696333)

What are Variations?
--------------------

Imagine you take a photo and make several copies of it. Now, you want to change each copy a bit to see different looks. Variations in Midjourney do just that for your generated images. They allow you to create different versions of the same image by changing little details or the overall arrangement.

Think of variations as a creative tool. They help you explore how several versions of your image might look, either by making major changes or just little tweaks, all without starting over from scratch.

#### Subtle Variations

Subtle variations make small, detailed changes to your image. This is perfect when you like the overall image but want to tweak small areas without a full redesign.

#### Strong Variations

Strong variations more significantly change your image while keeping the main theme intact. The core idea stays, but the visuals change in new ways. This is ideal for exploring bold, creative possibilities while sticking to the original concept.

Using Variations
----------------

*   Start by clicking on any image you've made on your Create or Organize page. This will open the image, revealing more options.
    
    Next, look for the "Creation Actions" section where you'll find the Vary options. Choose Subtle or Strong and your variations will immediately start generating.
    
    If you can't find the Vary options right away, just click "More options" and add a checkmark next to Vary to make them visible.
    
    ![web-vary.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32695143395085)
    
    If you'd like to change your prompt while making variations, check out our article on [Remixing](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32799074515213)
    .
    
*   Once your image is generated, you can create variations from the grid by using the `V1` `V2` `V3` `V4` buttons for your favorite image. These buttons follow the variation mode set in your settings. To check or switch this mode, use the [settings command](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32868982949517)
     and select `🎨 Strong Variation Mode` or `🎨 Subtle Variation Mode`.
    
    You can also make variations after upscaling your image. Once upscaled or separated from the grid, `🪄 Vary (Strong)` and `🪄 Vary (Subtle)` buttons appear, ready to use.
    
    If you'd like to change your prompt while making variations, make sure to turn on [Remix Mode](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32799074515213)
     in your [settings panel](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32868982949517)
    . Once on, a window will pop up after pressing the variation buttons, allowing you to edit the prompt.

---

# Repeat – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32757107922061-Repeat#page-container)

Generate multiple image sets from a prompt using the repeat parameter: --repeat or --r

### Want to generate multiple image sets from a single prompt? Use the repeat parameter: `--repeat` or `--r`

What is Repeat?
---------------

Every time you submit a prompt to Midjourney, you'll get a unique image—even if you use the same prompt. With the repeat parameter, you can tell Midjourney to run your prompt multiple times. For example, if you want three sets of images from the same prompt, just add `--r 3` to the end of your prompt.

The number of repeats you can use depends on your [subscription plan](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/27870484040333)
. Basic plan users can pick 2 to 4 repeats, Standard allows 2 to 10, and Pro and Mega plans offer 2 to 40. Just remember, the repeat parameter only works in [Fast and Turbo modes](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741)
. It won't work in Relax mode.

Each image set you create with repeat uses up [Fast GPU time](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741)
, just like running individual prompts. Using repeat can quickly consume your available GPU time, so it's important to keep track of how much time you have left.

Setting the Repeat Value
------------------------

*   Add `--r #` to the end of your prompt in the Imagine bar.
    
    ![web-imagine-prompt-repeat.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32760477886605)
    
    Note: Unlike other parameters, the repeat parameter will be stripped out of your finished images, so you won't see it once your images are done generating. This also means if you re-run the prompt you will have to manually add the repeat parameter again.
    
*   Add `--r #` to the end of your prompt in Discord.
    
    ![discord-imagine-prompt-repeat.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32760422861709)
    
    After sending your prompt, the bot will ask you to confirm the number of repeats and you'll need to click Yes before your prompts will run.
    
    Note: Unlike other parameters, the repeat parameter will be stripped out of your finished images, so you won't see it once your images are done generating. This also means if you re-run the prompt you will have to manually add the repeat parameter again.

---

# Stealth Mode – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32019750070669-Stealth-Mode#page-container)

### You can manage who sees your creations on the Midjourney website by using Stealth Mode.

What is Stealth Mode?
---------------------

Stealth Mode lets you control who can see your images and videos on the Midjourney website. You can choose which content to make public (publish) or keep private (unpublish).

Important: Even with Stealth Mode turned on, any creations made in public channels on Discord or rooms on web are still visible to others. If you want total privacy, use your web Create page, generate them in Discord [direct messages](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32637339216013)
, or work in a [private Discord server](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32637946450445)
 while using Stealth Mode.

Stealth Mode is available only to Pro and Mega plan members. If you cancel or downgrade your subscription, any content you've unpublished will stay that way on the site.

Switching to Stealth Mode
-------------------------

Your website and Discord settings are synced. This means that if you change your settings in one place, they'll automatically change in the other—including Stealth Mode. Double-check your settings to make sure they're set the way you want them before you generate images and videos!

*   **With Parameters:** To change your default setting for a specific prompt, just add the `--stealth` or `--public` [parameter](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32859204029709)
     at the end of your prompt in the Imagine bar.
    
    ![web-imagine-prompt-stealth.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32020608677517)
    
    **With Settings:** You can turn Stealth Mode on or off through the settings panel, which you can access with the settings ![settings-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32020421824013) button in the Imagine bar. Changing your default mode will apply to all your future prompts but won't affect your existing images.
    
    Note: Images and [videos](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/37460773864589)
     each have their own settings.
    
    To see which of your creations are public, visit your Organize page and use the filter checkboxes to select Published images.
    
*   **With Commands:** Use `/stealth` or `/public` as a standalone command in Discord to switch between Stealth Mode and Public Mode.  
      
    **With Settings:** Use the [settings command](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32868982949517)
     and turn the `🧍‍♂️Public Mode` button on or off from the menu. When the button is green it means you are in Public Mode. When the button is gray it means you are in Stealth Mode.  
      
    Changing your default mode will apply to all your future prompts but won't affect your existing images.  
      
    **With Parameters:** To change your setting for a specific prompt, simply add the `--stealth` or `--public` [parameter](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32859204029709)
     at the end of the prompt.  
      
    To confirm which mode you're in, use the [info command](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32084927086861)
     in Discord and check your Visibility Mode.

Unpublish Existing Creations
----------------------------

Upgrading to a subscription plan with Stealth Mode lets you unpublish images and videos you made before, even if they were created under a lower-tier plan. But keep in mind, upgrading or setting Stealth Mode as your default doesn't automatically make your public creations private. You'll need to manually unpublish them to make them private.

#### Individual Images/Videos

To change the visibility of an individual image or video, click into it from your Create or Organize page and use the options button ![options-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32022922203533) located near the prompt text.

![mj-web-unpublish.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32022985493133)

#### Multiple Images/Videos

To change multiple images and videos all at once, go to your Organize page. You can click and drag or use shift + click to select multiple items. Once you've selected them, look for the More button in the bulk change pop-up window at the bottom of the screen. This will allow you to make bulk changes easily.

![mj-website-archive-page-bulk2.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32023019959693)

No, hiding and unpublishing are not the same. Hiding an image or video on the website only makes it invisible to you—it remains public, and other users can still view it.

---

# Info Command – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32084927086861-Info-Command#page-container)

Use the /info command to see your subscription type, renewal date, and more.

![discord-user-info-command.png](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/muegen/midjourney_billing/main/images/docs/discord-user-info-command.png)

### Use the `/info` command in Discord to see information about your current queued and running jobs, subscription type, renewal date, and more.

![discord-user-info-command.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32085029154317)

Accessing your info panel lets you see useful information about your account and subscription plan easily within Discord. Here’s how to find it:

1.  Open your Discord app and go to the message box. Make sure you are in a server or channel that the Midjourney Bot has permission to access.
2.  Type `/` in the message box. You’ll see a list of commands pop up above.
3.  Keep typing until you see `/info`. This helps narrow down the options, just like a search field.
4.  Once you spot `/info` in the list, click it. If you aren't seeing any Midjourney commands, try our [command troubleshooting tips](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32894521590669)
    .
5.  Press Enter or Send to execute the command.

![discord-midjourney-info.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32894033836429)

Now, look out for your info panel; it’ll pop up right in your message feed. 

Only you can see your info panel, even if you enter the command in a public channel.

Info Details
------------

#### Your Info - Username

This is your Discord username. Keep in mind that your username can be different than your display name. If you need to contact our support staff, it's most helpful to provide your username.

#### User ID

This is your Midjourney User ID, which is unique to you and your subscription plan. If you need to contact our support staff, it's extremely helpful to provide this ID.

#### Subscription

The Subscription section shows which [plan](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/27870484040333)
 you are currently subscribed to and your next renewal date. Your renewal date and time is also when your monthly Fast time will refresh. 

#### Visibility Mode

This indicates whether you are currently in [Public or Stealth Mode](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32019750070669)
. Stealth Mode is only available to Pro and Mega Plan subscribers.

#### Fast Time Remaining

This shows your remaining [Fast GPU time](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741)
, shown as X / Y. The first number (X) tells you how much Fast time you currently have, and this includes any extra time you've bought or been awarded. The second number (Y) shows how much Fast time your plan gives you each month. Remember, your plan’s Fast time refreshes each month, and any leftover time won't roll over to the next month.

#### Ranking Count

This shows your total number of [ranked images](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/28014817524109)
, along with the number of images ranked in the last 30 days.

#### Lifetime Usage

This shows your lifetime Midjourney stats. Images include all types of generations (initial image grids, upscales, variations, remix, etc).

#### Fast, Turbo and Relaxed Usage

This shows your [Fast, Turbo and Relaxed Mode](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741)
 usage.

#### Queued Fast and Relaxed Jobs

Here you can view the number of prompts/jobs in your queue.

#### Running Jobs

This will list all prompts/jobs currently running.

---

# Prompt Basics – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32023408776205-Prompt-Basics#page-container)

A prompt is your creative starting point—learn how to turn words into unique and exciting images!

### A prompt is your creative starting point—learn how to turn words into unique and exciting images!

What is a Prompt?
-----------------

Creating an image with Midjourney starts with a "prompt." A prompt is simply the text or phrase you use to tell Midjourney what kind of image you want.

Your prompt could be just one word or a complete phrase. The more thought you put into your prompt, the more unique and interesting your image can be. So, take a moment to think about what you want to see, and use your words to guide Midjourney's creative process.

![imagine-prompt.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/36980789189645)

Prompting Tips & Tricks
-----------------------

Short and simple prompts typically generate the best images with Midjourney. Use phrases that clearly describe what you want to see. Think of it like giving a quick snapshot of your idea. Avoid making long lists or detailed instructions; these can confuse the process.

 **![thumb-down-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32069789621133)**Show me a picture of lots of blooming California poppies, make them bright, vibrant orange, and draw them in an illustrated style with colored pencils

 **![thumb-up-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32069789623437)**Colored pencil illustration of bright orange California poppies

#### Choose the Right Words

The words you pick matter! Try using specific synonyms. For example, instead of "big," consider "huge," "gigantic," or "enormous." Being precise can help get better results.

#### Be Specific with Numbers

Plural words like "cats" can be vague. Instead, use specific numbers like "three cats." Or go for collective nouns like "flock of birds" instead of just "birds."

#### Focus on What You Want

Describe what you do want instead of what you don’t. If you mention a party with “no cake,” a cake might still appear. For excluding items, read about the [no parameter](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32173351982093)
.

#### Prompt Length and Details

Your prompts can be simple—even a single word or emoji works. Short prompts let Midjourney's default style fill in the gaps. But if specific elements are important to you, be sure to include them. Fewer details mean more variety, but you get less control over the outcome.

Be clear about details that matter to you. Here are some areas to consider:

*   **Subject:** Who or what? (person, animal, character, location, object)
*   **Medium:** In what form? (photo, painting, illustration, sculpture, doodle, tapestry)
*   **Environment:** Where? (indoors, outdoors, on the moon, underwater, in the city)
*   **Lighting:** What kind? (soft, ambient, overcast, neon, studio lights)
*   **Color:** In what shades? (vibrant, muted, bright, monochromatic, colorful, black and white, pastel)
*   **Mood:** Feelings to evoke? (playful, calm, gloomy, energetic)
*   **Composition:** How is it framed? (portrait, headshot, closeup, birds-eye view)

Advanced Prompts
----------------

Once you're comfortable with basic prompts, start exploring more advanced options! Add one or more [Image Prompts](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32040250122381)
, use multiple text phrases, and apply tools called [parameters](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32859204029709)
. These give you the ability to create more complex or specific images. Experiment by mixing different elements to boost your creativity!

![web-imagine-prompt-advanced.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32023852788621)

**Text Prompt**  
The text description of what you want to see. Keep reading for prompting tips and tricks. Well-written prompts help generate amazing images! 

**Image Prompts**  
Adding images to your prompt influences the style and content of your new creations. You can do this through [Image Prompts](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32040250122381)
, [Style References](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32180011136653)
, and [Character References](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32162917505293)
.

**Parameters**  
[Parameters](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32859204029709)
 are tools that let you customize how an image is generated. They can adjust things like [aspect ratios](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/31894244298125)
 to tailor your image to your liking. Parameters get added to the end of your prompt. 

More Prompt Help
----------------

Midjourney has a vibrant community that loves problem-solving and helping others! If you need more help or tips, make sure to visit our [Prompt Craft channel on Discord](https://discord.com/channels/662267976984297473/992207085146222713)
 or the [Prompt Craft Room](https://www.midjourney.com/rooms/44a30f92-a8c1-470b-a553-86f49add2a7a)
 on web.

Need Help Getting Started?  
  
[Getting Started Guide](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33329261836941)

---

# Personalization – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32433330574221-Personalization#page-container)

Create custom image styles with personalized profiles and moodboards using --p

### Create custom image styles with personalized profiles and moodboards using `--p`

![personalize-header-new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/37436501709197)

What is Personalization?
------------------------

Personalization acts like a style assistant for your image creations. By liking or ranking images and creating moodboards, Midjourney gets to know what kind of images you love and uses that information to generate images tailored to your personal tastes and unique style.

Personalization is compatible with Midjourney [versions](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853-Version)
 6 and 7. 

Unlocking Personalization
-------------------------

Unlocking your Global Personalization Profile is the first step to using Personalization.

**Here’s how to unlock your Global Profile:**

1.  Visit the [Personalize](https://www.midjourney.com/personalize)
     page and find your Global V7 Profile.
2.  Click the "Continue ranking" button.  
    ![unlock-personalization.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/37436476293517)
3.  You’ll see two images. Click on the one you prefer.
4.  A new pair of images will appear. Keep picking your favorites.
5.  As you choose, watch the progress bar move at the top of the page. Once you’ve ranked enough pairs, your profile will unlock.

![rank-pairs.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/37436476295309)

To get the most out of your personalization profile, we recommend spending more time ranking images. The more images you rank, the better Midjourney gets at tailoring the images to your style.

Using Personalization
---------------------

*   Add `--p` to the end of your prompt in the Imagine bar. This will automatically apply your default personalization profile to your prompt.
    
    To use a specific profile, go to the Personalization page, hover your mouse over a profile and click the "Use Profile" button to add its profile ID to the Imagine bar (example: `--p pID`). You can also use a specific code `--p code` from a previous prompt.
    
    ![imagine-prompt-personalize-web-new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35577121023629)  
    
    You can choose a default profile for all your images in the personalization panel. To do this, click the personalization ![p-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35577114322957) dropdown button in the Imagine bar, turn Personalize on, and select your preferred profile. Once you set it, this will apply to all your future prompts.
    
*   Add `--p` to the end of your prompt in Discord. This will automatically apply your default personalization profile to your prompt.
    
    To use a specific profile, copy its ID from your [Personalization page](https://www.midjourney.com/personalize)
     using the "Use Profile" button and add it to the end of your prompt (example: `--p pID`). You can also use a specific code `--p code` from a previous prompt.
    
    ![discord-imagine-prompt-personalize.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32433804268301)
    
    On Discord you can use the `🙋 Personalization` button in your Midjourney [settings](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32868982949517)
     to automatically add the `--p` parameter to all your prompts.
    

You'll only be able to use personalization once you've ranked enough image aesthetic pairs and/or ❤️ed enough images from the Explore page. If you try to use `--p` without enough data, you'll see an error message directing you to do more ranking.

Personalization Profiles
------------------------

You can create multiple profiles, each with a different style or mood. Each profile has a unique ID that generates a code when used in your prompts.

Create and manage your personalization profiles on your [Personalize page](https://www.midjourney.com/personalize)
.

![new-personalize-page2.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/37436476297741)

#### ![global-profile-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32434314881037) Global Profile

This is your default profile, and each Midjourney [version](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853-Version)
 has its own Global Profile. You'll need to unlock this profile by ranking images before you can create additional profiles. When ranking for your Global Profile, try to avoid "skipping" as much as possible—more data results in a better tuned Global Profile.

Liking ❤️ images from other users on the Explore page will influence your Global Profiles. Check which version the liked image was made with to see which Global Profile it will affect.

#### ![standard-profile-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32434298550029) Ranked Profiles

These are extra profiles you can create to focus on specific styles. You rank pairs of images to show Midjourney what you like.

If you Rank Image Aesthetics from the [Tasks](https://www.midjourney.com/tasks)
 page, this information will automatically apply to your Global Profile. To rank more images for a specific profile, locate it on your [Personalize](https://www.midjourney.com/personalize)
 page and click its name.

#### ![image-prompt-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32434210841101) Moodboard Profiles

You create these by selecting specific images that set a particular mood or vibe. You can upload your own images, provide image URLs, or select images from your gallery.

Creating Personalization Profiles
---------------------------------

*   ![personalize-walkthrough1.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32468305257741)
    
    Head to the [Personalize page](https://www.midjourney.com/personalize)
     on the Midjourney website to view and manage your personalization profiles. This is your starting point for customizing your image styles.
    
*   Turn on personalization using the toggle switch. This will automatically add your default personalization profile to all your prompts.
    
    ![personalize-walkthrough2.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32466563423757)
    
*   To create a new ranked profile, click the "Create Ranked Profile" button.
    
    This will take you to a new page where you'll rank pairs of images. Choose the image you like best between the two options.
    
    Continue ranking until you've unlocked your profile, which is necessary before you can start using it.
    
    ![personalize-walkthrough3new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35577121022477)
    
*   To create a moodboard profile, click the "Create Moodboard" button.
    
    This will take you to a blank moodboard page. Here, you can upload images from your computer or device, add images from URLs, or add images from your Midjourney gallery.
    
    ![personalize-walkthrough4new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35577114321677)
    
*   Hover your mouse over a profile and click "Use Profile" to add your profile ID to the Imagine bar.
    
    ![personalize-walkthrough5new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35577114322445)
    
    If you've turned on personalization, you can also use the "Select" button on your favorite profile to set it as your default profile.
    

Personalization Codes
---------------------

Your personalization profiles will grow and change as you keep liking and ranking more images. As your profile updates, it will generates new codes that act like labels for the different versions of your profile.

Copy the ID from your profile to use the latest version. To find older codes, you can use the `/list_personalize_codes` command in Discord or revisit your previous prompts to see the codes you used before.

Note: When using a profile ID it will automatically convert from `--p pID` to `--p code` when you submit your prompt.

Managing Your Profiles
----------------------

You can manage your profiles by renaming or deleting them. To do this, click the three dots icon and use the pencil ![pencil-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32674819046413) button to rename it or the trash can ![trash-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32674833345293) button to delete it.

When you delete a profile it disappears from your profiles list, and you won't be able to add any new data to it. However, any codes that were already created from that profile will still work, allowing you to continue using its style in future prompts.

![manage-profile.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35577121024525)

Stylize with Personalization
----------------------------

When using personalization, the [stylize parameter](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32196176868109)
 controls how much of your personalization is applied to the image. A lower stylize value will limit the personalization, while a higher value will increase it. The stylize parameter accepts values from 0 to 1000. The default is 100.

![personalize-stylize-examples-new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/37436501723021)

Need Help Getting Started?  
  
[Getting Started Guide](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33329261836941)

---

# Text Generation – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32502277092109-Text-Generation#page-container)

Generate images with words and phrases in them using quotation marks.

### Add words to your images with double quotation marks!

![Two images of cyberpunk cats with neon signs that say 'Midjourney' creating using a prompt with double quotation marks](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32502493621389)

Text in Images
--------------

When you use Midjourney [versions](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
 6 and later, you can get words or phrases to show up in your images by putting them inside double quotation marks (" "). For instance, if you want to create an image of a cyberpunk cat with a neon sign that says Midjourney, just surround "Midjourney" with quotation marks in your prompt.

Important: You need to use double quotation marks—single quotes or apostrophes (' ') won't work for this.

#### Best Practices

Text generation works best with the standard Latin alphabet, like English letters. If you stick to shorter words or phrases, you'll have a better chance of getting them to appear just right. It's also helpful to include things like "with the words" or "text" or "written" in your prompt.

If you encounter issues with getting the text exactly how you want it, consider using [Raw Mode](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32634113811853)
 or lowering the [Stylize](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32196176868109)
 value. You can also use the [Editor](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32764383466893)
 on web or try the [Vary Region](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32794723105549)
 feature in Discord to fix minor glitches.

#### ![thumb-down-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32502615481741) Bad Prompt Examples:

a logo with the company name Boing  
put the text 'Hello' in a frame

#### ![thumb-up-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32502615484557) Good Prompt Examples:

a pastel watercolor landscape with "imagine" written in the clouds  
a cartoon drawing of a manual with the words "read the docs" in big text on the pages

More Prompt Help
----------------

Midjourney has a vibrant community that loves problem-solving and helping others! If you need more help or tips, make sure to visit our [Prompt Craft channel on Discord](https://discord.com/channels/662267976984297473/992207085146222713)
 or the [Prompt Craft Room](https://www.midjourney.com/rooms/44a30f92-a8c1-470b-a553-86f49add2a7a)
 on web.

# Quality – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32176522101773-Quality#page-container)

Control the processing time of your images with the quality parameter: --quality or --q

### Control the detail and processing time of your images with the quality parameter: `--quality` or `--q`

![quality-header-new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/37914513293965)

What is Quality?
----------------

Quality controls how much [GPU time](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741-GPU-Speed-Fast-Relax-Turbo)
 is spent making your images. This can change how the details and textures look.

In Midjourney [version](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
 7 the default setting for quality is 1. You can also set values to 2 or 4, which will use 2 times or 4 times more GPU time.

Keep in mind, the quality parameter only influences the first set of four images you create. It doesn't affect later [variations](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32692978437005)
, [inpainting/outpainting](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32764383466893)
, or [upscales](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32804058614669)
.

If you're looking to save on GPU time, give [Draft Mode](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/35577175650957-Draft-Conversational-Modes)
 a try.

Setting the Quality Value
-------------------------

*   Add `--q #` to the end of your prompt in the Imagine bar.
    
    ![Using --q on midjourney.com](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32177966686477)
    
*   Add `--q #` to the end of your prompt in Discord.
    
    ![Using --q in Discord](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32177966689293)
    

*   • In version 7 there is no `--q 3` setting. If used, it will automatically switch to `--q 4`  
    • `--q 4` is not compatible with [Omni Reference](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/36285124473997-Omni-Reference)
    .

---

# Using Folders – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/34580542725645-Using-Folders#page-container)

Use folders to keep your creativity organized and make dedicated spaces to generate your images.

### Keep your creativity organized with folders!

What are folders?
-----------------

Folders work just like the folders on your computer, helping you organize and manage your Midjourney creations. You can set up individual folders and even group them to keep things organized. Here's how you can make the most of folders:

*   **Organize Your Images:** After creating images, you can sort them into different folders—imagine a filing system for your various projects or styles. Feel free to name folders any way you like, as long as each has a unique name.
*   **Generate Images Inside Folders:** You can also generate images directly within a specific folder. This ensures any new creations are automatically saved where you want them, keeping related images together in an easy-to-find place.

You can access folders from both the [Create](https://www.midjourney.com/imagine)
 page and the [Organize](https://www.midjourney.com/archive)
 page. Just click the folder button next to the search bar to open the folder menu, and click it again to close it.

![folders-new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34583852932749)

To create a new folder, open the folder menu and click the "New Folder" button. Type in a unique name for your folder and press enter on your keyboard. Your new folder will appear in the menu, with a number showing how many images it contains.

Adding & Removing Images
------------------------

Head to the [Organize](https://www.midjourney.com/archive)
 page to easily add images to your folders.

*   #### Adding Multiple Images at Once:
    
    1.  To select multiple images, hold the Shift key on your keyboard and click the images one by one. Or, click and drag your mouse over the images you want.
    2.  With your selection ready, make sure the folder menu is open, and drag the selected images onto a folder.  
          
        Alternatively, with your images selected, use the bulk actions menu at the bottom of the screen. Click "More," then "Add to Folder," and choose your desired folder.
    
    ![bulk-select-tools.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34584428269325)
    
*   #### Adding an Individual Image:
    
    Click and drag the image to your folder in the folder menu or right-click the image, select "Add to…" and pick your folder.
    
    #### Removing Images:
    
    Open the folder by clicking on it. To remove multiple images, select them and use the bulk actions menu: click "More," then "Remove from Folder." To remove a single image, right-click it and choose "Remove from…"
    
    ![right-click-add.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34585362846861)
    

We used to have a feature called Smart Folders that automatically organized images based on search terms. These have now become Saved Searches, which you can learn more about in our [Organizing Your Creations](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33329462451469-Organizing-Your-Creations#h_01JMGG77RJ9C9Z66HF8TAE0MPM)
 article.

Generating in Folders
---------------------

Creating images directly inside a folder is easy and helps keep your work organized in dedicated creative spaces.

1.  **Enter the Folder:** First, click the folder from the folder menu to open it and go inside. When you are inside a folder the folder button next to the search bar will display the name of your current folder, so you always know where your work is being stored.
2.  **Start Generating:** Use the Imagine bar at the top of the screen to start generating your images. While you're inside a folder, the Imagine bar will have an indicator below it that says "Generating in..." to show where your images are going.  
    ![create-in-folders.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34584268558733)
3.  **Stop Generating in the Folder:** To stop generating images in a folder, you need to leave the folder. Do this by looking for the folder button next to the search bar and clicking the "X" next to the folder name. Even if you navigate to another page on the website, your prompts in the Imagine bar will continue to save in the folder until you leave it.

Managing Folders & Groups
-------------------------

#### Rename

To change a folder's name, hover over the folder to reveal the three dots icon. Click on it to open a small menu where you can select "Rename." Once you've entered the new name, press enter on your keyboard to save it.

#### Delete

To delete a folder, hover over the folder to reveal the three dots icon. Clicking it will open a small menu where you can select "Delete." Deleting a folder won’t delete the images inside. They will remain safe in your gallery.

#### Download

Need to download all the images in a folder? Simply hover over the folder to reveal the three dots icon, click it, and select "Download" from the small menu. 

![folders-menu.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34583914644237)

#### Folder Groups

If you want to create a folder group, open the folders menu and click the "New Folder Group" button. Type the desired name for your group and press enter to save it.

Organizing your folders is as easy as dragging and dropping them into or out of groups. You can also use the three dots icon menu on a folder and select "Move to" and pick the group.

Remember, folders that aren't in any group will always appear at the top of the folder menu. Additionally, if you remove all folders from a group, that group will automatically be deleted.

---

# Earning Free Fast Time – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/28014817524109-Earning-Free-Fast-Time#page-container)

Looking to add more Fast time to your account? Midjourney provides a few ways to earn extra Fast time, perfect for keeping your creative projects going! Just remember, you'll need an active subscription to use any awarded time, and it expires 30 days after it's given. You can also [purchase additional Fast time](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33570952624141)
 on our website.

#### Ranking Images

Each day, the top 2,000 users who rank the most images receive an extra hour of Fast time free. If you're among the top rankers, you’ll receive a direct message from the Midjourney Bot in Discord around midnight UTC. Curious about how to rank images? Check out our [Complete Tasks](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33390759197197)
 article for more details.

#### Surveys

Occasionally, we conduct surveys and offer Fast time as a reward. The amount you can earn varies, so keep an eye on the [Tasks](https://www.midjourney.com/tasks)
 page to find open surveys and see how much Fast time you can gain.

# Character Reference – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32162917505293-Character-Reference#page-container)

Use the same character in multiple images and scenes using character references.

### Want to use the same character in multiple images and scenes? You can provide Midjourney with a Character Reference!

![character-ref-header-new.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35587406260877)

Character Reference is not compatible with [version 7](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
, please use [Omni Reference](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/36285124473997)
 instead.

What is a Character Reference?
------------------------------

A Character Reference allows you to recreate a specific character in multiple images.

By using a picture of a character you like, Midjourney can recognize the character's features, like hair color, clothes, and facial traits, and use these details for generating the character in new scenes. This helps maintain consistency across different images. 

Using a Character Reference
---------------------------

*   To add an image to your prompt, start by clicking on the image ![image-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458993421) icon in the Imagine bar. This opens the images panel, allowing you to upload new images or pick from those you've already uploaded.
    
    ![new-character-ref-ui.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/35587413100429)
    
    Drag and drop your image from the uploads library into the Character Reference section. To remove your image from the Imagine bar, hover your mouse over it and click the X icon.
    
    If you want to use your images with multiple prompts, click the lock icon ![lock-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34019527842445) to keep your images pinned to the Imagine bar.
    
    **Image Reference Types:**  
    ![image-prompt-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32365078878477) [Image Prompt](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32040250122381)
     (default)  
    ![style-reference-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32365078888589) [Style Reference](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32180011136653)
      
    ![character-reference-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168806889741) [Omni Reference](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/36285124473997)
     (replaces Character Reference)
    
*   To use a Character Reference in Discord, start by adding the `--cref` parameter to the end of your prompt, then pasting your image URL. If you want to use multiple images, separate each URL with a space.
    
    ![discord-cref.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32169938615309)
    
    It's important to ensure that you have a valid image URL, meaning the image should already be online. If your image is stored on your computer or device, you can [host it on Discord](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32558957919117)
     to generate an image URL.
    

Best Practices
--------------

*   **Use Midjourney Images:** For best results, start with an image of a single character created by Midjourney. Images of real people typically won't look exactly like them.
*   **Limit Character References:** While you can use more than one image of the same character, it's often not necessary.
*   **Account for Details:** Be aware that intricate details like specific freckles or logos on clothing might not come out exactly right.
*   **Use Detailed Text Prompts:** Combine your character reference with a clear text prompt. Text is just as important for conveying the full scene and additional details beyond what the reference image shows.

#### ![thumb-down-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458988941) Bad Prompt Examples:

![image-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458993421) put this man in a cafe  
![image-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458993421) add this man to a cafe setting

#### ![thumb-up-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458999565) Good Prompt Examples:

![image-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458993421) a man with blue hair and gold glasses sitting in a cafe  
![image-icon.svg](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32168458993421) illustration of a man sitting alone in a cafe

Character Weight
----------------

Character weight acts like a dial that lets you choose how much detail from your reference image shows up in your new image.

By default, with `--cw 100`, Midjourney includes as much detail as possible, like the face, hair, and clothing. If you turn the dial down to `--cw 0`, the focus will mainly be on the character's face. This gives you the flexibility to adjust how much detail is pulled from your reference image.

Midjourney uses Image Prompts and References as inspiration to guide new creations, not to copy them exactly. If you're not getting exactly the results you want, check out the [Editor](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32764383466893)
.

*   • For your prompts to work, you need a text prompt in combination with your Character Reference.  
    • Your image file should end in .png, .gif, .webp, .jpg, or .jpeg.  
    • Character Reference can be used with Midjourney and Niji version 6.  
    • Character Reference can be combined with [Style References](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32180011136653)
     and [Image Prompts](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32040250122381)
    .

Need Help Getting Started?  
  
[Getting Started Guide](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33329261836941)

---

# Permutations – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32761322355597-Permutations#page-container)

Use permutation prompts to generate multiple prompt variations from a single idea.

### Explore endless combinations! Use permutation prompts to easily generate multiple prompt variations from a single idea.

![permutation-header.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32762671903629)

What are Permutations?
----------------------

Think of permutation as a way to make many different prompts from just one prompt. It helps you swap certain parts—like colors or items—within your prompt to create different versions. Instead of typing each one by hand, you write it once, putting your options in curly braces {} separated by commas, and let Midjourney do the rest.

For example, if you prompt `a {red, green, yellow} bird`, Midjourney will swap out "red," "green," and "yellow" in separate prompts to give you three different prompts:

1.  `A red bird`
2.  `A green bird`
3.  `A yellow bird`

You can use permutations on any part of your prompt, including [parameters](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32859204029709)
. For instance, if you want to try the same prompt in multiple [aspect ratios](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/31894244298125)
, you can use `--ar {1:1, 2:3, 3:5}`.

The number of permutations you can use depends on your [subscription plan](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/27870484040333)
. If you have the Basic plan, you can create a maximum of 4 prompts with a single permutation prompt. The Standard plan allows you up to 10. For Pro and Mega plans, you can go up to 40. Just remember, permutations only work in [Fast and Turbo modes](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741)
. They won't work in Relax mode.

Each individual prompt you create with permutations uses up [Fast GPU time](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32016412137741)
, just like running individual prompts. Using permutations can quickly consume your available GPU time, so it's important to keep track of how much time you have left.

Using Permutations
------------------

*   Put the variables you want to change inside curly braces {} in your prompt in the Imagine bar. Make sure to separate them with commas.
    
    ![web-imagine-prompt-permutation.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32762896602637)
    
*   Put the variables you want to change inside curly braces {} in your prompt in Discord. Make sure to separate them with commas.
    
    ![discord-imagine-prompt-permutation.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32762896604941)
    
    After sending your prompt, the bot will ask you to confirm the number of permutations and you'll need to click Yes before your prompts will run.
    

*   It is possible to use multiple sets of bracketed options in a single prompt. For example, `a {red, green} bird in the {jungle, desert}` will produce four prompts.
    
    It is also possible to nest sets of bracketed options inside other sets of brackets within a single prompt. For example, `A {bird {on a pier, on a beach}, dog {on a sofa, in a truck}}` will produce four prompts.
    
    You can also use permutations on parameters. For example, `a red bird --v {4, 5, 6.1}` will produce three prompts each in a different version of Midjourney.
    
    Permutations can be used in [custom suffixes and option sets](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32868982949517)
    .
    
    If you want to include a comma within the curly brackets that does not act as a separator, place a backslash `\` directly before it. For example, `{red, pastel \, yellow} bird` will produce two prompts:  
    `a red bird`  
    `a pastel, yellow bird`

---

# Image Size & Resolution – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33329374594957-Image-Size-Resolution#page-container)

From pixels to prints: Master Midjourney image sizes and resolution.

### From pixels to prints: Master Midjourney image sizes and resolution.

![image-size-header.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/33393852389133)

Let's dive into what you can expect with your Midjourney images, how to handle them, and how resolution works. By the end, you'll know how image sizes affect your work and what steps you can take for printing.

What Is Image Size?
-------------------

Every Midjourney image starts with a certain number of pixels, measured width by height. For example, when you use the default 1:1 [aspect ratio](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/31894244298125)
, Midjourney [version](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
 7 creates [upscaled images](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32804058614669)
 that are 2048 x 2048 pixels (px). Pixels are the tiny dots that make up your image, much like the tiny tiles in a mosaic.

Understanding Resolution
------------------------

Image resolution represents the level of detail in an image. For printed images, resolution measures the density of ink dots per inch (DPI). 

When you open a Midjourney image in a program like Photoshop, the resolution will probably be 72, which is just right for online or screen use. There are no "high-resolution" image files for screens like monitors or phones. What matters is how many pixels you have versus the size of the screen. So, an image fits differently on a small phone compared to a large monitor based on its pixel count.

![MJ_ImageSize_Resolution_screenSize.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/33393159209613)

The same image dimension viewed on different screens.

Why Resolution Matters for Printing
-----------------------------------

When you want to print an image, the DPI affects its clarity and size on paper. While 72 DPI looks sharp on your screen, printing usually requires around 300 DPI for the best quality. This is because printed images need many more dots squeezed into each inch to look just as clear as they do on your screen.

How to Change Resolution
------------------------

If you want a higher DPI for your Midjourney images, here are some steps to help you along:

*   **Use Editing Software:** Programs like Photoshop let you change the DPI. Open your image, find the image settings, change the DPI to 300, and check that "Resample" is off. This keeps your pixel dimensions the same (2048 x 2048px), but now it's ready for a higher-quality print.
*   **Third-Party Upscaling Tools:** Sometimes you'll need your image to have more pixels to keep it sharp as you make it larger. You can use third party upscaling tools to upscale your image, which adds more pixels and helps maintain clarity at a higher DPI.

Can You Print a Midjourney Image?
---------------------------------

Absolutely! You can print your Midjourney images, but the quality of the print follows the rules of DPI. For a sharp, quality print, aim for 300 DPI. So, with a default 2048 x 2048px image from Midjourney, you can produce a good quality 6.8 inch by 6.8 inch print (2048 pixels divided by 300 DPI equals 6.8 inches).

If you want to print larger than 6.8 inches, you can lower the DPI, but be aware that your image might not print as clear or sharp, and some printers may have minimum DPI requirements. For example, some posters can be printed at 150 DPI and still look clear because they are viewed from further away. Alternatively, use third party upscaling tools to add more pixels, increasing your image dimensions for larger prints while maintaining clarity.

#### Need More Help?

A great place to find recommendations is our [Midjourney community on Discord](https://discord.gg/midjourney)
. Members often share tips and experiences on which tools they prefer!

---

# Aspect Ratio – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/31894244298125-Aspect-Ratio#page-container)

Midjourney images start as squares, but you can change this using the aspect ratio parameter: --aspect or --ar

### Midjourney images start as squares, but you can change this using the aspect ratio parameter: `--ar` or `--aspect`

![Examples of images in different aspect ratios overlaid on a grid](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/31926773524877)

What is Aspect Ratio?
---------------------

Aspect ratio is a way to describe how wide and tall an image is. It's shown as two numbers, like 1:1 or 4:3, that tell you how the width compares to the height. For example, a 4:3 aspect ratio means the width is 4 parts, and the height is 3 parts.

By default Midjourney images are square, meaning the width and height are the same, so the aspect ratio is 1:1.

Choosing an aspect ratio helps you decide if your image will be wide (landscape) or tall (portrait). Use a bigger first number for a wide image and a bigger second number for a tall image.

Important: Aspect ratio isn't the same as image dimensions. The final size of your Midjourney images will also depend on the [Midjourney version](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
 and [Upscaler](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32804058614669)
 you're using.

Setting the Aspect Ratio
------------------------

*   Add `--ar #:#` to the end of your prompt in the Imagine bar.
    
    ![Using --ar on midjourney.com](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/31921155358861)
    
    You can choose a default aspect ratio for all your images in the settings panel. To do this, click the settings ![Settings Icon](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/31921336789645) button in the Imagine bar. Once you set it, this will apply to all your future prompts.
    
*   Add `--ar #:#` to the end of your prompt in Discord.
    
    ![Using --ar in Discord](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/31920468751373)
    

**1:1** – Perfect square, popular for social media profile pictures and posts.  
**4:3** – Slightly rectangular, used in older TV screens and computer monitors.  
**2:3** – Common in printed photography and picture frame sizes.  
**16:9** – Widescreen, the standard for HD videos and most modern TVs.  
**9:16** – Vertical orientation, common for mobile content on social media.

*   To find the aspect ratio of an image, use its dimensions. For example, if your image is 1920x1080 pixels, enter `--ar 1920:1080`, and Midjourney will simplify it to `--ar 16:9`. For something like 8.5x11 inches, remove the decimals (Midjourney doesn’t accept them) and enter `--ar 85:110`. This makes it easy to match your image's proportions.

*   You can change a generated image's aspect ratio using the [pan](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32570788043405)
     and [zoom out](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32595476770957)
     tools on both the web and Discord, or by using the [Web Editor](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32696720371341)
     on midjourney.com

*   • The default aspect ratio is 1:1.  
    • `--ar` cannot contain decimals. Use 139:100 instead of 1.39:1.  
    • Some aspect ratios may be slightly changed when upscaling.  
    • Older Midjourney [versions](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
     may not support all aspect ratios.  
    • Extremely wide and tall aspect ratios are experimental and may produce unpredictable results.

---

# Cookie Policy – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/37012090959245-Cookie-Policy#page-container)

Last Updated: May 29, 2025

This Cookie Policy explains how Midjourney uses cookies and similar technologies on the Site and Services (as defined in the [Privacy Policy](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32083472637453-Privacy-Policy)
), and how you can manage your cookie preferences.

Cookies and Similar Technologies
--------------------------------

Cookies are small text files that may be placed on your device when you interact with certain websites and services. They are widely used to support key website functions like logging-in, remembering your account preference, and enhancing user experience. In this policy, we use the term “cookies” to also include similar technologies like web beacons and embedded scripts that help us automatically collect certain usage data.

Types of Cookies
----------------

Midjourney uses the following types of cookies:

**Essential Cookies**: These types of cookies are necessary for the Site and Services to function properly. They help enable core features like secure login, session management, and navigation. Because these cookies are required for use of certain features and functionalities, they are always active and cannot be disabled.

**Analytics Cookies:** These cookies help us understand how visitors interact with our Site and Services, such as which pages are most popular or which features are the most engaging. This information helps us improve performance and usability of our Site and Services.

Advertising Cookies: These types of cookies are used to measure the effectiveness of our marketing campaigns and help deliver relevant content and advertisement to users. These cookies may be set by us through our Site or Service or by our advertising partners.

Managing your Cookie Preferences
--------------------------------

You can manage your cookie preferences at any time through the [Privacy Settings](https://www.midjourney.com/profile-settings)
 page. There, you can choose which types of cookies to allow or disable. Please note that essential cookies cannot be disabled, as they are required for the Site and Services to operate.

Most web browsers provide settings that let you control or block cookies. You can usually configure your browser to notify you when a cookie is being set, or to automatically disable or delete cookies. Please note that disabling cookies, especially essential cookies, means that certain features of our Site and Services may not function properly. For more details about cookies and how to manage them across different browsers, please visit [allaboutcookies.org](https://allaboutcookies.org/)
.

---

# Purchasing Extra Fast Time – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33570952624141-Purchasing-Extra-Fast-Time#page-container)

If you run out of Fast time before your subscription renews, you can easily purchase more to continue creating without delays.

1.  **Visit the Manage Subscription Page:** Log in to midjourney.com and head over to the [Manage Subscription](https://www.midjourney.com/account)
     page. This is where you can find all the details about your plan and purchase extra Fast time.
2.  **Purchase Additional Hours:** Click the "Buy more Fast hours" button and select the amount of Fast time you wish to add. Keep in mind, these purchased hours come with a 60-day expiration, so plan accordingly.  
    ![purchase-fast-time.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/34267586140941)
3.  **Active Subscription Needed:** To use purchased Fast time, you must have an active subscription. If your subscription lapses, the extra Fast time won't be available unless you renew your plan.
4.  **Non-Refundable:** Once you've purchased the additional Fast time, it cannot be refunded.

You may also be able to [earn free Fast time](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/28014817524109)
 by [completing tasks](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33390759197197)
 on our website.

# Pan – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32570788043405-Pan#page-container)

Use pan to expand the canvas of your image and fill in new details.

### Want to explore beyond your image's borders? Use Pan to grow the canvas with new detail!

![pan-header.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32571779733773)

What is Pan?
------------

Imagine you have a framed photo and you want to make the frame bigger without changing the picture itself. Panning expands the "canvas" of your image in a direction you choose. The extra space is then filled with new details that match the original image, using guidance from your prompt. It's a cool way to explore and add context to your picture while keeping the core parts untouched.

Pan is compatible with Midjourney [versions](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
 5 and later, however when using V7, Pan still utilizes V6.1.

Using Pan
---------

*   Start by clicking on any image you've made on your Create or Organize page. This will open the image, revealing more options.
    
    Next, look for the "Creation Actions" section where you'll find the Pan options. Choose any of the arrow buttons to quickly expand your image in the direction you want.
    
    If you can't find the Pan options right away, just click "More options" and add a checkmark next to Pan to make them visible.
    
    ![Pan options buttons on midjourney.com](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32572616587661)
    
    If you'd like to change your prompt while panning to add new elements, click the "Editor" button. This loads your image into Midjourney's editor, where you can make multiple changes at once (pan, [zoom](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32595476770957)
    , [remix](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32799074515213)
    , and [vary region](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32794723105549)
    ). You can click and drag the canvas edges or select a different [aspect ratio](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/31894244298125)
     to pan.
    
    ![Editor button on midjourney.com](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32572616589069)
    
    For more detailed guidance, check out our article on the [Editor](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32696720371341)
    .
    
*   After your image is generated, use the `U1` `U2` `U3` `U4` buttons to separate your favorite image from the initial grid. Once separated, use the `⬅️` `➡️` `⬇️` `⬆️` arrow buttons to quickly expand your image in the direction you want.
    
    If you'd like to change your prompt while panning to add new elements, make sure to turn on [Remix Mode](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32799074515213)
     in your [settings panel](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32868982949517)
    . Once on, a window will pop up after pressing the Pan buttons, allowing you to edit the prompt.

---

# Zoom Out – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32595476770957-Zoom-Out#page-container)

Zoom Out of your creations to shrink the original image and reveal new content.

### Pull back the lens and reveal the bigger picture with Zoom Out!

![zoom-out-header.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32599827091341)

What is Zoom Out?
-----------------

Take an image you've generated and make it look like you're backing away to reveal a wider view! Imagine your original image getting smaller, while new content appears around it, all based on your original creation and prompt—without altering the original image.

One thing to note is that when you zoom out, it doesn't change the actual size of your image in pixels—it's all about the cool visual effect. It's like giving your image more room to breathe and explore!

Zoom out is compatible with Midjourney [versions](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32199405667853)
 5 and later, however when using V7, Zoom out still utilizes V6.1. Zoom values can range from 1.0 to 2.0.

Using Zoom Out
--------------

*   Start by clicking on any image you've made on your Create or Organize page. This will open the image, revealing more options.
    
    Next, look for the "Creation Actions" section where you'll find the Zoom Out options. Choose from 1.5x or 2x to quickly zoom out your image. To use a custom zoom value, simply hover over the 2x button. You'll see a pencil ![Pencil Icon](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32596609569165) icon pop up. Click it, and you can enter the zoom value you want between 1.0 and 2.0, then click the button to generate your image.
    
    If you can't find the Zoom Out options right away, just click "More options" and add a checkmark next to Zoom Out to make them visible.
    
    ![Zoom Out options buttons on midjourney.com](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32596567019661)
    
    If you'd like to change your prompt while zooming out to add new elements, click the "Editor" button. This loads your image into Midjourney's editor, where you can make multiple changes at once ([pan](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32570788043405)
    , zoom out, [remix](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32799074515213)
    , and [vary region](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32794723105549)
    ). You can click and drag the corners of your image or use the Scale slider to zoom out.
    
    ![Editor button on midjourney.com](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/32595665910797)
    
    For more detailed guidance, check out our article on the [Editor](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32696720371341)
    .
    
*   After your image is generated, use the `U1` `U2` `U3` `U4` buttons to separate your favorite image from the initial grid. Once separated, use the `🔎 Zoom Out 2X` or `🔎 Zoom Out 1.5X` buttons to quickly zoom out your image.
    
    **Custom Zoom**  
    If you'd like to change your prompt while zooming out or use a custom zoom value, use the `🔎 Custom Zoom` button. This will open a text window where you can change your prompt text and [parameters](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32859204029709)
    , as well as set a custom zoom value between 1.0 and 2.0, before submitting your prompt.
    
    Pro Tip: You can use Custom Zoom to change the aspect ratio of a generated image by setting the zoom level to 1 (so it will not zoom) and adding or changing the aspect ratio in the prompt text.
    
    **Make Square**  
    If your image has a non-square shape (using a custom [aspect ratio](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/31894244298125)
    ), you'll see a `Make Square` button, allowing you to quickly zoom so that your new image is square. Your image will expand either horizontally or vertically depending on your image's starting aspect ratio.

# Logging In & Connecting Accounts – Midjourney

[Skip to main content](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33390994570509-Logging-In-Connecting-Accounts#page-container)

Whether you're joining us for the first time or you're a returning user, it's important to sign in with the correct account. This helps make sure you can enjoy using Midjourney on both our website and Discord without any issues. Every [subscription plan](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/27870484040333)
 lets you use both platforms—it's all about setting things up correctly.

New Subscribers
---------------

If you’re new here, we’re excited to have you! Here’s how you can create an account:

1.  **Visit the Home Page:** Go to midjourney.com and click the **Sign Up** button.
2.  **Choose a Sign-Up Method:** You’ll see two options to sign up...
    *   **Continue with Discord:** Pick this option to use Discord for creating images.  
        • You can link either an existing Discord account or make a new one.  
        • Your Discord login details will serve as your Midjourney credentials. This means you’ll use the same credentials for both Discord and our website, so make sure your [Discord account is verified](https://support.discord.com/hc/en-us/articles/6181726888215-How-to-Verify-Your-Discord-Account)
         and keep track of your email and password.
    *   **Continue with Google:** Choose this option to sign in to midjourney.com with your Google account.  
        ![web-login.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/33475715041421)
3.  **Connect Your Account:** If you continue with Google, you’ll be prompted to enter your Google login details. If you continue with Discord, you’ll need to enter your Discord login details. You'll also be asked to authorize Midjourney to access your Discord account.  
      
    Important Note for Discord Users:  
    If you're linking an existing Discord account, double-check the email address associated with it. Entering an email that isn't linked to a Discord account will prompt Discord to take you through the steps of creating a new account. This could lead to complications if you already have an account.
4.  **Add a Second Sign-In Method (optional):** After setting up your account or subscribing, you can add the other sign-in option, like adding Google if you started with Discord, and vice versa. Simply go to your [Account Settings](https://www.midjourney.com/profile-settings)
     page on midjourney.com. However, if your Discord account has already created Midjourney images, you’re considered a returning user and you need to sign in with Discord.

Right now, you can create a Midjourney account using either a Discord account or a Google account. We don't have the option to create a username and password specific just to Midjourney. You will need to use Google or Discord as your login method.

Returning Subscribers
---------------------

Welcome back to Midjourney! If you've used our service before, even just a free trial, chances are it was before August 2024. Back then, Discord was the only option for account creation. To access your old image history and ensure a smooth experience, it’s crucial to sign in with your Discord account first.

Warning: If you sign in with Google and create a new subscription, you will not be able to connect a Discord account with past image history.

**How to Reconnect:**

1.  **Visit the Home Page:** Go to midjourney.com and click the **Log In** button.
2.  **Sign In with Discord:** To link up with your past images and activity, start by logging in with your Discord account. You'll also be asked to authorize Midjourney to access your Discord account.  
    ![discord-login-authorize.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/33475416756365)  
    Important Note for Discord Users:  
    Double-check the email address associated with your Discord account. Entering an email that isn't linked to a Discord account will prompt Discord to take you through the steps of creating a new account. This could lead to complications if you already have an account. Before clicking "Authorize," double-check that your correct Discord username is shown at the top of the popup. If the username is incorrect, use the "Not you?" link. 
3.  **Add Google as a Login Option (optional):** Once you're logged in, you can add Google as a login option by visiting your [Account Settings](https://www.midjourney.com/profile-settings)
     page. This way, you’ll have the flexibility to use either method in the future.

Remember, starting with your Discord login is key to ensuring that everything syncs correctly. Once you're all set, feel free to explore and create new images. Welcome back and happy creating!

Connecting Accounts
-------------------

All our [subscription plans](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/27870484040333)
 allow you to use Midjourney both on our website and in Discord. But if you want to make images in Discord, you will need to have a Discord account connected to your Midjourney account. You can do this, as well as add a Google login, on your [Account Settings](https://www.midjourney.com/profile-settings)
 page on midjourney.com

![manage-profile.png](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/article_attachments/33476280397453)

In the "Connected Accounts" section, you'll find your login methods displayed along with their details. If a login method isn't connected yet, you will see a "Connect" button next to it. Just click this button to proceed with linking your account.

#### Midjourney ID

Your Midjourney ID is also shown on this page. When you contact billing support, providing this ID is really helpful and highly encouraged. This helps us assist you more quickly and effectively.

#### Disconnecting Accounts

Accounts can only be disconnected by our billing support team. If you need help with this, please [reach out to billing support](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32638309968141)
. You may be required to verify your account ownership before your login method can be disconnected. Your account must have one method connected at all times, so make sure you have a secondary method already connected before contacting support.

Troubleshooting
---------------

If you're having trouble connecting your accounts or logging in, you might see a message like this:

#### **"One of the accounts you are trying to link has a subscription while the other already contains jobs. At this time, linking such accounts is not supported."**

This often occurs if you log into midjourney.com using Google, subscribe to a plan, and then try to connect a Discord account that has already created images with Midjourney. Each account now has its own image gallery, so they can't be linked or connected.

**Solutions:**

1.  **Use a Different Discord Account:**  
    Try connecting a Discord account that hasn't used Midjourney before.
2.  **Cancel and Switch Accounts:**  
    If eligible, [cancel and refund your subscription](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/25386088618253)
    . Log out of the website, then log in with your Discord account and re-subscribe (see [Returning Subscribers](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33390994570509-Logging-In-Connecting-Accounts#h_01JHJRQBY1WZTQ76QAENFCYJYK)
    ).
3.  **Contact Billing Support:**  
    [Reach out to our billing support team](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32638309968141)
     for further assistance.

#### **  
"Another account already exists for \[EMAIL\]. Please log in with that account and then link it."**

This means there’s already an account registered with that email address.

**Solutions:**

1.  If you encountered this error while trying to log in with Google, try logging in with the Discord account that uses the same email address instead. Once logged in, you can link your Google account on your [Account Settings](https://www.midjourney.com/profile-settings)
     page.
2.  If you see this error while trying to log in with Discord, try logging in with Google using the same email instead. Once logged in, go to your [Account Settings](https://www.midjourney.com/profile-settings)
     page and connect your Discord account.
3.  [Reach out to our billing support team](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/32638309968141)
     for further assistance.

  
  

Need Help Getting Started?  
  
[Getting Started Guide](https://docs.midjourney.com/hc/en-us/articles/33329261836941)
